PARLIAMENT OF TASMANIA 
DEBATES OF THE HOUSE OF ASSEMBLY 
 
 
 
 
DAILY HANSARD 
 
 
Tuesday 2 December 2025
Preliminary Transcript 
 
 
 


 
 
 
 
This draft transcript of debates is issued in advance of the final Hansard for the use of the members of the House of Assembly and copies made from this may not be protected by parliamentary privilege. 
 






Tuesday 2 December 2025

The Honourable Speaker, Mrs Petrusma, took the Chair at 10.00 a.m., acknowledged the Traditional People, and read Prayers.


LEAVE OF ABSENCE

Member for Prosser - Mr Vincent

Mr ROCKLIFF (Braddon - Premier) - Honourable Speaker, I advise the House that Minister Vincent will be absent from Question Time today due to illness. I will be taking questions with respect to his portfolios.


Member for Clark - Mr Willie

Ms FINLAY (Bass - Deputy Leader of the Opposition) - Honourable Speaker, similarly, I advise the House this morning that the Leader of the Labor Party, Josh Willie, is unwell and not here today.


QUESTIONS

North Launceston Football Club - Funding

Ms FINLAY question to MINISTER for SPORT, Mr DUIGAN

During Estimates, you admitted to withdrawing an offer of $100,000 to the North Launceston Football Club because the president appeared with Labor at a media event. It's less than two years before you kick them out and now you've withdrawn the funding, you're effectively leaving them without a home. York Park has been their home for over 100 years. Why are you punishing a community organisation simply for standing with another political party?

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank the member for the question. I take this opportunity to recognise the great work and the important place that the North Launceston Football Club has in the football landscape of Tasmania; a proud club, 103 years old. I am committed to them having a home in the short, medium and long term, and that's why we have established a working group which includes all the relevant stakeholders - the club, Launceston City Council, Stadiums Tasmania, and the Northern Tasmanian Football Association - and that working group has been working through the options for North Launceston going forward. 

Obviously we will see a very seismic change in the football landscape in Tasmania from next year, with the introduction of VFL football and, of course, from 2028 with our AFL and AFLW teams. UTAS Stadium will be a critical piece of infrastructure in that story, and there is a $130 million upgrade at that stadium going on now.

To your question, the North Launceston Football Club is having its annual general meeting on Wednesday, as I understand it, at which time and through the work of the working group they will be contacting my office and me and we will be looking forward to understanding what is the long-term future for North Launceston but, as I say, I am committed to an outcome for the club, as is the government.

Supplementary Question

Ms FINLAY - A supplementary question, Speaker?

The SPEAKER - I will hear the supplementary question.

Ms FINLAY - My question was very clear about the minister punishing a community organisation for standing with another political party. He didn't go anywhere near the question. My question to the minister is do you think it's appropriate to punish a community organisation for standing with another political party?

The SPEAKER - Honourable Minister for Sport.

Mr DUIGAN - To the detail of your question, those were absolutely discussions that were happening in the context of an election. I was in communication with the football club -

Mr Mitchell - You signed a letter.

The SPEAKER - Order, the honourable member for Lyons.

Mr DUIGAN - I put my thoughts down on paper and shared them with the club and various others and was looking for feedback. Shortly thereafter, I think the club decided that it preferred another option and that's the way it went. That's exactly what happened and I stand here committed to providing an outcome for North Launceston Football Club.


North Launceston Football Club - Funding

Ms FINLAY question to MINISTER for SPORT, Mr DUIGAN 

[10.06 a.m.]
Clearly, that deserves a second question to the Minister for Sport to put some facts on the record. You say you were thinking about it, minister. The fact is that your chief of staff sent a letter to the club president, Adrian Hall, and stated that the Liberal government would provide the club with $100,000 to plan for their future. Mr Hall says he only learned through the media following your train wreck of an Estimates attempt that the funding would be axed. That's not thinking, minister, that's commitments in writing. Did you or your chief of staff ever tell Mr Hall that the offer put in writing had been withdrawn simply because they stood with Labor for a photo? 

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank the member for the question. As I say, we stand here, I've put my thoughts on paper, we are committed to finding a way forward for the North Launceston Football Club. I met with Mr Hall at UTAS Stadium last week or at some stage and we talked about that and about him taking his club and his membership through the journey, through the work of the working group, to understand what options exist for the club. If there is an ask of government, it doesn't exist at the moment. If there is an ask of government, we will absolutely consider that. As I say, I stand committed to resolving the future of the North Launceston Football Club, as does this side of government, and we will make sure that -

Members interjecting.

The SPEAKER - Order. Sorry, minister. I remind the honourable members of the opposition that you need to allow the minister to respond. He still has two more minutes to address your question, so I ask that you listen to him with respect. I remind everyone of your badges, to show respect too. 

Mr DUIGAN - Thanks, Speaker. As I say, we are committed and I am committed, as Minister for Sport, to sort this out and provide a home for North Launceston going forward and I hope to have more to say on this in the very short term, as -

Mr WINTER - Point of order, Speaker, Standing Order 45, relevance. The question is very clear. It asks whether Mr Duigan or his chief of staff ever told the club that they'd withdrawn the funding offer. I ask you to bring him back to the question.

The SPEAKER - Thank you, honourable Minister for Sport.

Mr DUIGAN - As I say, those discussions were part of an election campaign. I was sharing my thoughts with the club, with members of the North Tasmania Football Association (NTFA) so they knew what the government or what I was interested in doing.

Members interjecting.

The SPEAKER - Order. Honourable members of the opposition, I will start issuing warnings and I remind members that they can occur very quickly. Warnings one, two and three can come within seconds, so I say to you all today to allow the ministers to respond, because we're going to have a respectful Question Time. 

Mr DUIGAN - Certainly, as I stand here, there's nothing in that letter that I resile from. I am happy to continue to work with the club.

Supplementary Question

Ms FINLAY - A supplementary question, Speaker?

The SPEAKER - I will hear the supplementary question.

Ms FINLAY - Minister, in that letter you indicated or the chief of staff indicated there would be $100,000 in funding for the club. I'd like you to confirm that you maintain your commitment to that if you say that you commit to everything that you put in writing. Speaker, the supplementary question is do you accept that Tasmanian sporting clubs, when provided a commitment from your government in an election, should be worried that if they talk to any other political party, whether the Greens or a member of the crossbench, they would be financially punished for doing so? Does that worry you, minister?

The SPEAKER - Honourable Minister for Sport. 

Mr DUIGAN - As I have said, I don't resile from anything that is in the contents of that letter. That was my position then.

What is really important to understand is that the club needs to decide what its position is, as it did on the days leading through the election when both parties were having conversations with the club. I don't resile from that, but I want to hear what the club has to say about this. It is important that the club -

Ms FINLAY - Point of order, Speaker, Standing Order 45, relevance. My supplementary was clear. Thank you, minister, for saying that you agree to the words that your chief of staff wrote to the club in terms of the $100,000. 

Mr Duigan - I didn't resile from it.

Ms FINLAY - You said that you agreed to the content of the letter and secondly - my point of order on the supplementary is, do you believe that all sports clubs in Tasmania should worry about the financial implications of talking to other members of this parliament?

The SPEAKER - Time has expired.


Macquarie Point - Contaminated Soil

Dr WOODRUFF question to PREMIER, Mr ROCKLIFF

[10.11 a.m.]
Last week in Legislative Council Estimates we caught Macquarie Point Development Corporation (MPDC) clearly misleading. We asked MPDC how much contaminated soil containing asbestos, lead, mercury, arsenic, cyanide and other chemicals of concern was under the footprint of your stadium and we were told is 130,000 cubic metres. When we later sought to confirm that amount with the Environment Protection Authority (EPA), we were told, in fact, it could be up to 220,000 cubic metres of contaminated soil - a significantly different number.

On Thursday, during the Legislative Council's hearing with the Tasmanian Planning Commission (TPC) panel members, we asked whether MPDC had told the TPC about this huge volume of toxic soil that will need to be excavated, treated, stored and removed from the site. They had not. Apart from the obvious public health risks posed by this large volume of soil. It raises a question of trust. Given the untruths, how can Tasmanians -

The SPEAKER - The member's time for the question has expired.

Members interjecting.

Dr Woodruff - trust a single word MDPC says or you do either?

The SPEAKER - Next question, because there wasn't a question - that was a long statement, Dr Woodruff. You need to - at the heart, you did not get to your question.

Dr Woodruff - My question was - it goes to a matter of trust, and I didn't get to the follow-up question.

The SPEAKER - No, sorry, you had to ask a question.

Dr Woodruff - Speaker, I have never heard that - there was a question there. There was a question about the trust.

The SPEAKER - You said, 'my question is' and the time expired. You had a very long statement.

Dr Woodruff - I had a second question. The question throughout was about trust - how can anyone trust the Premier?

The SPEAKER - You are asking the question now. I remind members asking a question that you have one minute to ask a question and 30 seconds to ask a supplementary. It is not a time for a statement, it is to ask a question. The question did not get asked in that long statement. I encourage members to make your questions shorter and time them if necessary, but the time is not to make a statement to the House. 


Cancelled Metro Services

Mr O'BYRNE question to PREMIER, Mr ROCKLIFF

[10.13 a.m.]
In August 2023, Metro cancelled 177 services across the Hobart network in what was described as a temporary adjustment. We're now two years on from that temporary adjustment and the 120 of those services remain cancelled. During Metro's scrutiny hearing last week, it was revealed that there were no plans to reintroduce these services, citing a Department of State Growth review. In 2023, we were told these cancellations were temporary. Metro have now confirmed the bleeding obvious - these services are permanently cancelled. Why did it take questions from me in scrutiny hearings for Tasmanians to discover that these bus services will remain cancelled, pending the outcome of a review - a review with no timeline?

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank the member for the question and his interest in this matter. Public transport is very important to all Tasmanians and it is essential for supporting Tasmanians get to where they need to be - work or recreation. We are very pleased we were able to support Tasmanians with half-price bus fares in the last 100 days, as part of our record of delivery. This has been some journey and I accept that you have been on this important matter for some time, Mr O'Byrne, including scrutiny last week.

The information that I have is that, in 2023 - the date that you referred to - Metro took the difficult step to suspend some of its less frequented services while maintaining its more popular services to reduce daily unexpected cancelled trips. Tranche two of the Metro service restoration started on 25 August 2025, restoring 29 services Monday to Thursday and 31 services on Friday. Together with the first tranche of restorations in November 2024, about 33 per cent of services originally suspended have now been restored. Metro's customer satisfaction has risen to 78 per cent in 2025 and that's increased in the last 12 months.

There is still a lot of work to do, I accept that. We're continuing on the greater Hobart network review and look forward to it being released for public consultation. The first phase of the review is due to come into effect in early 2026 and this will involve adjustments to the existing Metro timetable to maximise the use of existing services. Metro runs more than 2300 trips every day across Tasmania and has been working hard to recruit more drivers to strengthen their workforce, which has been a challenge. I will look in greater detail in terms of the response to your question. I will consult the minister, who's not able to be here today, but we are committed to improving the frequency, reliability and consistency of public transport networks across Tasmania.
———————————————————
Recognition of Visitors

The SPEAKER - I would like to ask all members to please join with me in welcoming to the House of Assembly TasTAFE ELICOS English language students. Welcome to parliament.

Members - Hear, hear.
———————————————————
Small Horticulture Producers - New Regulations

Prof RAZAY question to MINISTER for PRIMARY INDUSTRIES and WATER, Mr PEARCE

[10.17 a.m.]
I refer to the proposed Primary Produce Safety (Horticulture Produce) Regulations 2025. Small market gardens and roadside stalls are big tourism attractions in Tasmania and are also extremely popular with the locals. They provide fresh produce directly from the garden to the consumer, which means their products are safer, fresher, and more nutritious than those from larger industrial growers. I am concerned that these new regulations will introduce stringent and costly new safety regulations, including significant paperwork and auditing requirements for small growers. Can the minister advise if the government is going to ensure that small growers do not have unfair and costly regulations imposed on them, so they can continue to provide fresh and nutritious produce at the market and roadside?

The SPEAKER - The members time for asking the question has expired.

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank the member for his question. The member is of course talking about the national body, Food Standards Australia New Zealand, applying a food safety regime, or some legislation, for those selling fresh produce from a roadside store and the like. That needs to fit in with every state and territory across the country. What we've said, and the approach that we've taken, is one of consultation. We want to hear from growers, be they small growers or large, about what their particular concerns are, and we need to know the level of their operation because that will determine the risk that is involved. The reason that this has come to pass is that, in the last couple of years, there have been up to 10 deaths related to salmonella. The good member will understand the risks with salmonella and like. We need to cover that. At the same time, we also need to make this applicable to a small store holder versus a large commercial grower.

That's the approach that we've taken, that's the feedback we're getting from the community. That is, they're suggesting now - and we've extended that consultation time to 19 December, and we've run PR campaigns to get that news out. We want to hear that information; we want to hear their points. That's out to 19 December, and in the new year we'll put this all together.

At this stage, the feedback we're getting is they need a tiered system. That's what they're asking for. We're hearing their voices loud and clear. We don't want one-size-fits-all. It needs to be tailored, but it needs to be safe. I look forward to, in the early part of the year, coming to the House with a form that will suit all. 


Concrete Sand Shortage

Mr GEORGE question to PREMIER, Mr ROCKLIFF

[10.21 a.m.]
The national body Cement Concrete & Aggregates Australia knew as far back as July that infrastructure costs in south-east Tasmania would soar as a result of the supply of suitable sand for concrete running out. How did it know? It knew because it had seen the Mineral Resources Tasmania (MRT) report warning of delays, cost increases, and the impact of having to ship suitable sand 300 kilometres from the north-east instead of 35 kilometres locally. The impact will be widely felt throughout the state's construction industry, but its impact on the Macquarie Point stadium will clearly be enormous. If the government knew of this shortage and of its impact, which it clearly did as far back as the July election, why did it conceal the report for months until the death knell of the stadium report?

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank the honourable member for his question. I reject his assertion. The matter about sand supply - sand and stone aggregates are the second-most heavily extracted resources globally, surpassed only by water. Local Tasmanian quarries supply the bulk of raw materials necessary to build critical infrastructure.

With a high volume of construction projects underway - that's a good thing - and planned across the state, it's essential that projects can access the materials they need, when they need them. The construction industry is currently experiencing strong growth, presenting both opportunities and, of course, challenges. There are always challenges with growth, but it doesn't mean we shouldn't grow.

MRT recently released a new technical report, I'm advised, a study of the sand inventory of southeastern Tasmania, as part of the government's 100-day election commitments. The technical sand report discusses the current status of the sand resources in south-east Tasmania. The study has confirmed that while Tasmania has abundant sand deposits overall, the greater Hobart area faces growing challenges to sourcing concrete-grade sand close to major construction and infrastructure hubs, I'm advised.

As previous reports have indicated, the sterilisation of land suitable for potential future sand sources is one of the reasons for supply constraints in the greater Hobart region. We will continue to work with relevant planning authorities to ensure extractive industries are considered when making land use planning decisions. The technical sand report will also help guide industry in exploring for future sand resources to meet rising demand.

That is the information that I have. I appreciate the member asking a question about an input into a building. We look forward to further construction - not just the Macquarie Point stadium, but homes, hotels, and all sorts of great things that our hard-working tradespeople will be able to do to continue building Tasmania.

Supplementary Question

Mr GEORGE - A supplementary question, Speaker?

The SPEAKER - I will hear the supplementary question.

Mr GEORGE - Premier, you have not answered my question. Why did the government sit on a Minerals Resources Tasmania document for four months, knowing its impact on the Macquarie Point stadium and also other infrastructure would affect costs throughout Tasmania and particularly on the stadium?

The SPEAKER - That is sort of going down a new path of enquiry. If the Premier has anything further to add?

Mr ROCKLIFF - I will just refer to our 2030 Strong Plan for Tasmania's Future, 100 days of delivery, 20 August, 28 November 2025, which I'm very proud of. I appreciate all the work our team has done in bringing this together. We've even, so detailed is this report, in actual fact, that it mentions sand. Here we go -

Dr Broad - Is it the head in the sand bit?

Members interjecting.

Mr ROCKLIFF - I'll give you that one, Shane. The first one I've given you in about seven years you've been here, but you got there, well done. That was good. 

Completed the investigation by Mineral Resources Tasmania into sand supply and released the report on the MRT website. The critical minerals prospectus - 

The SPEAKER - The honourable Premier's time has expired.


North Launceston Football Club - Funding

Ms FINLAY question to MINISTER FOR SPORT, Mr DUIGAN

[10.26 a.m.]
I have to ask another question to the Minister for Sport, because I now have a second letter to North. This one was sent in February, so they've been working on this for a long time. It was sent to the club on 28 February 2025, and it says: 

It's not my intention that North will be left without a home. 

Yet isn't that exactly what you're doing? You need to apologise for this absolute shambles. Can't you see that it won't be possible for North to operate out of Invermay Park by the end of 2027 if they can't get to work on planning and design before next year, which is months before you're going to chuck them out of their home - a home they've had for 100 years?

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank the member for the question. I think that probably only emphasises the fact that we are committed to finding a home for North Launceston, to working with the club on their long-term future prospects. 

Ms FINLAY - You committed $100,000, minister, then took it away. It's childish behaviour.

The SPEAKER - Order. The honourable acting Leader of the Opposition has asked a question. The minister has two-and-a-half minutes to answer it. Honourable minister, please continue. I ask that he's allowed to answer it in silence, please. 

Mr DUIGAN - As I have said, we will be very much guided by the club, by its members and what they would like to see for North Launceston going forward. The AGM will be held this Wednesday. I met with the president on Thursday last week in follow-up to all of this. We will work our way through this. They will not be left without a home. That will not be the case. We will work with the club, with Stadiums Tasmania, and we will find a way forward. 

It's important to also recognise that there are other stakeholders involved in this work. The City of Launceston Council, who is a co-owner of the University of Tasmania York Park precinct, is a very important stakeholder. We need them to be engaged with this. This is work that will continue, and we will get an outcome.


Supplementary Question

Ms FINLAY - I have a supplementary question, Speaker.

The SPEAKER - I will hear the supplementary question.

Ms FINLAY - In his answer, the minister referred to other stakeholders and their role in this. He has referred to the fact that the President of North Launceston Football Club, their members, their players and all their supporters have done their job and have been doing it for a really long period of time. 

What the minister hasn't said in his answer is how will you make that happen when you made a written commitment of $100,000 to allow them to do this work, to find and secure a home beyond 2027? You put it in writing and you withdrew it because they stood with the Labor Party. How will you make sure that they have a home before 2027?

The SPEAKER - The honourable member's time has expired. Honourable Minister for Sport.

Mr DUIGAN - I am, the government is, committed to making sure that North Launceston is accommodated. In regard to those discussions, they were made during a campaign. An official commitment was not made. That's an important part - an official commitment was not made. I am committed to working with all parties.


Tasmanian Active Infrastructure Grants Program

Mr GARLAND question to MINISTER for SPORT, Mr DUIGAN

[10.30 a.m.]
In February of this year, you invited Tasmanians to submit applications for grants from a $5 million fund associated with the Tasmanian Active Infrastructure Grants Program. Applications for this round of grants closed on 30 April 2025, with successful applicants to be notified by 29 August 2025. We know you recently withdrew a sporting grant to North Launceston Football Club because it didn't stick to the Liberal government's script, but surely not all the applicants for these grants were Labor supporters? Why has your government not announced the outcome of the grants?

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank the member for the question. The Tasmanian Active Infrastructure Grants Program is a really important program. It is one of the large grants programs that we run and enables clubs to access up to $500,000, so it makes really meaningful impacts to clubs, particularly in and around the area of upgrading change rooms and all those sorts of things. We're seeing infrastructure across the state which was built some time ago that perhaps didn't necessarily contemplate what we're seeing in the development of sport now, particularly when it comes to junior athletes and women and girls playing sport. I'm very pleased to have our Women and Girls in Sport Strategy imminently out in the public realm.

The issue with the grants round as it applied to this calendar year was the fact that, thanks to Mr Winter and others, we had an election brought into the middle of the year and that has necessitated a change to the way the grants have been rolled out and assessed. The announcement in our next 100-day plan announced the successful recipients of the Active Tasmania Infrastructure Grants. That work will happen through the month of December.


Macquarie Point - Contaminated Soil

Ms BURNET question to MINISTER for MACQUARIE POINT URBAN RENEWAL, Mr ABETZ

[10.33 a.m.]
We learnt at Estimates and from the Tasmanian Planning Commission (TPC) hearing provided to the upper House that the Macquarie Point site contains up to 220,000 cubic metres of contaminated fill containing asbestos, lead, mercury, arsenic, cyanide, benzenes and other toxic chemicals. This is information the Macquarie Point Development Corporation (MPDC) apparently didn't provide to the TPC. It was confirmed by the Environment Protection Authority (EPA) that the regulated cap on the Copping C Cell is 45,000 cubic metres. If your stadium was to go ahead and construction begin, a significant public health issue is raised. 

What's the plan? It's clear to us that you and the MPDC can't be trusted to tell the truth about the contaminated soils on site. As minister responsible for the stadium, how do you explain MPDC's misleading information, and can you give any assurance that this high volume of contaminated soil can be safely dealt with?

The SPEAKER - The member's time has expired.

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I wish I could thank the member for Clark for the question, but the aspersions cast on very good public servants is something that should not be occurring in this place. By all means, attack me, attack members of the government, but don't attack public servants who cannot defend themselves in this place.

We are asked to accept at face value the numbers provided by the Greens. Last Sunday, there was a group of 15,000 people gathered and the Greens tell us that was equivalent to the 1500 that appeared the week before, so I am very sceptical, forgive me, but experience has taught me to be exceptionally careful when Greens quote numbers and assert things because I've been burnt once too often, so I will be exceptionally careful. However, let's also be exceptionally clear -

Dr Woodruff - Get to the question, get to the Hansard, get to the truth.

The SPEAKER - Dr Woodruff.

Ms BURNET - Point of order, Speaker, Standing Order 45, relevance. I draw the minister to the question.

The SPEAKER - I ask the honourable Treasurer to be relevant to the question, please.

Mr ABETZ - I thought I was, but I can understand that the answer is uncomfortable for the member for Clark. What I would say to the member for Clark, even assuming that which you assert is correct - let's assume that just for once, very dangerous, I know, but we will assume it - that contaminated soil would need to be removed, irrespective of the project that was going to take place on the site. Indeed, Labor and the Greens at one stage wanted a hospital there, all on contaminated soil. Having the odd concert, convention or football game compared to a hospital was not an issue for the Greens at the time. It's only become an issue because they don't like the AFL stadium and the multipurpose nature of it.

Dr Woodruff - You need three more Coppings.

The SPEAKER - Dr Woodruff.

Mr ABETZ - I'm further advised the testing undertaken by the MPDC indicates that approximately 10 per cent of the historical fill estimated to be removed will require disposal at Copping, and this is well within the facility's annual capacity. The MPDC has drilled I don't know how many hundreds of holes on the site to determine the levels of contamination. Isn't it amazing when we refer to the site as an 'industrial wasteland' the Greens attack us for referring to it as such, but then when it suits them they say the whole site is contaminated and how dare you build anything on it. I just wish there was some consistency.

The SPEAKER - The honourable Treasurer's time has expired.

Supplementary Question

Ms BURNET - A supplementary question, Speaker?

The SPEAKER - I will hear the supplementary question. 

Ms BURNET - The question I asked was what's the plan? I draw the minister's attention to what was put on the public record, that there is about 220,000 cubic metres of contaminated fill. What's the plan, because Copping won't be able to take all of that?

The SPEAKER - Honourable Treasurer.

Mr ABETZ - Speaker, it's one of those problems when you have a supplementary question and you want to ask it without listening to the answer. I just indicated to you that Copping can take the amount. I will repeat it again for the benefit of the honourable member. I'm further advised that testing undertaken by MPDC indicates that approximately 10 per cent of the historical fill estimated to be removed will require disposal at Copping. This is well within the facility's annual capacity.

Dr Woodruff - That's not what they said to the Legislative Council.

The SPEAKER - Dr Woodruff.

Mr ABETZ - Leader of the Greens, we know that the member for Clark had to ask your question because you didn't quite get around to it, but that doesn't give you licence to interject on the answer. What I would say to the member for Clark is that the contamination will be removed by all the required standards and the people who use that facility can be guaranteed that they will be safe and there is no human health issue.

The SPEAKER - The honourable Treasurer's time has expired.


North Launceston Football Club - Funding

Mrs GREENE question to PREMIER, Mr ROCKLIFF

[10.38 a.m.]
Your Sports minister admitted in a budget Estimates hearing that he cancelled funding for the North Launceston Football Club because the club president stood next to Labor in the media. Last year, the former Sports minister cancelled a large event at Mudbar because the owner supported a Labor policy. This is a pattern of behaviour from your government. Do you think it's acceptable for a minister to retaliate against a local football club for engaging with another political party? Does this behaviour meet your ministerial code of conduct?

ANSWER

Honourable Speaker, I thank Mrs Greene for the question and I appreciate your commitment to your electorate and sporting infrastructure across the wonderful electorate of Bass. I don't agree with how you've characterised the matters you've raised. We are working with all Tasmanians, irrespective of who they may support at the ballot box. We treat all Tasmanians equally in terms of the services they require or ask for. Of course we cannot deliver on 100 per cent of what comes across our desk but we do our very best to support -

Members interjecting.

Macquarie Point Stadium - Interest on Borrowings

Ms JOHNSTON question to TREASURER, Mr ABETZ

[10.43 a.m.]
 [Bookmark: Phr15_O=174.1_D=29.4_C=0.73] Former Treasury secretary, Martin Wallace, in his capacity as a TPC panellist on the stadium, last week confirmed to Legislative Council members some shocking truths. He said that within five years of borrowings to fund the stadium build, Tasmanians will be paying a $90 million interest bill in that year alone. He said the debt burden was 'a completely untenable situation.' Do you agree with Mr Wallace? If you don't, and dismiss Martin Wallace's, former head of  [Bookmark: Phr16_O=204.3_D=13.7_C=0.84] Treasury, expert advice as just another opinion, then will you please show and table your numbers to prove him wrong? 

ANSWER

 [Bookmark: Phr17_O=220.4_D=12.4_C=0.84] Honourable Speaker, I thank the honourable member for the question. With respect, I do disagree with Mr Wallace and the figures he presented. As a former secretary, of course, you listen [Bookmark: Phr18_O=233.1_D=30.0_C=0.80]  to him, but one also takes up-to-date advice and the considerations. 

From our perspective as a government, what we are looking towards is seeking to grow the economy, and that is why the stadium is so fundamentally important. A brand new payroll coming into this state of $44 million, a brand new hotel - if not two - the expansions that are being considered right around the waterfront on the basis of  [Bookmark: Phr19_O=263.4_D=22.4_C=0.82] the stadium being approved. There is, if I might say, a divergence of views in relation to that, but I am backing in - with the 15,000 that were outside this place on Sunday - that there is the opportunity to grow our economy with this proposal.

In relation to the  [Bookmark: Phr20_O=287.8_D=5.1_C=0.79] interest payments that will be required, if you take into account  [Bookmark: Phr21_O=293.4_D=11.6_C=0.89] the budget and the amount that we are borrowing - and I am on record, we are borrowing too much - but the big question is, and that is something that has to be considered - is the borrowing for the net operating activities of government or something that will last for decades and generations to come, that you can look down the camera barrel and say, 'I don't mind if my kids and my grandkids keep on helping to pay for this piece of infrastructure, because they're going to get a full lifetime out of it, I won't.' Therefore, there is, in my humble opinion, a divergence of views. If you're building something for the future that is multigenerational and something which is for the here and now, that is fundamentally different. 

I believe I tabled an answer, or provided an answer, in relation to the interest payments that will be made. I can provide that in further detail, but I think I've already tabled it. We are looking at the debt servicing cost estimate on equity transfer state funding of $113,000 in 2024-25 through to $3 million, or $3.321 million, in 2031-32. In the scheme of things, this stadium is going to be less than one per cent of our budget, but it will be so transformative. That is what has to be considered and understood. 

You can always find fault with any new proposal. What I encourage people to do is grab the opportunity.

Mornington Roundabout - Update

Mr WINTER question to INFRASTRUCTURE and TRANSPORT, Mr VINCENT

My constituent lives in Mornington on thee shore and points out that, despite the many promises about the Mornington roundabout for many years, nothing has actually happened. He points out that there's been no progress updates on this issue for many years. He has discovered that the promised federal funding has been allocated, but the state Liberal government has still not built anything. He asks when will the promised Mornington roundabout upgrade be finally delivered so that residents can have a safe intersection to travel?


Salmon Industry - Impact on Marine Environment

Dr WOODRUFF question to PRIMARY INDUSTRIES and WATER, Mr PEARCE

My question is from Mary Kate in Cygnet, who's so concerned about the effects of salmon farming in her area that she and other members of her local swimming group are worried about going into the water. They're sick of the salmon industry destroying the health of their waters, whether it's diseased and dying fish washing up on their beaches or now the florfenicol that's coating feed and being dumped in large quantities.

The Cygnet Sea Urchins are cold water swimmers and they've had to move their swims to Kingston and some have stopped swimming altogether. They swim for physical and emotional health, which is impossible due to these impacts. They want to know when you will restore their beautiful local marine environment and ask whether you will rein in the industry and require it to move, destock all fallow salmon pens to stop the antibiotic being dumped into waterways.


Public Transport - Completion of Claremont Park and Ride

Mr VERMEY question to MINISTER for INFRASTRUCTURE and TRANSPORT, Mr VINCENT

My constituents in Clark, in particular the northern end, have special interest in finding out about the public transport and asking when the Claremont Park and ride will be completed and can the minister provide an update.


Frankford Highway - Upgrades

Ms DOW question to Minister for INFRASTRUCTURE and TRANSPORT, Mr VINCENT

My question is to the Minister for Infrastructure. Can you please provide an update for my constituent from Wynyard on the upgrades that the government proposes to do with the Frankford Highway with detailed timelines?


PETITION

Ice Skating in Tasmania

[11.16 a.m.]
Ms JOHNSTON (Clark) - Honourable Speaker, I have the honour to be the bearer of an e-petition signed by approximately 1111 petitioners. Petition conforms with the relevant standing orders and rules of the House. The petition of the undersigned citizens of Tasmania draws to the attention of the House that Tasmania's only ice rink closed in May 2022. The petitioners request the House to call on the Tasmanian government to honour its commitment agreed to by the House of Assembly on 18 October 2023 to determine and announce a site for a new facility by 31 December 2025 and provide the necessary funding and begin the build in 2026. 

Petition received.

[11.30 a.m.]
Mr BARNETT (Lyons - Attorney-General) - Honourable Speaker, I'm more than happy to reflect upon the matter of public importance put forward by Labor today and do not concede or consent in any way, shape, or form with the allegations put by the Deputy Leader for the Labor Party in this House earlier today and in the few moments prior to my rising. These are clearly allegations to besmirch the reputation of the Minister for Sport, and indeed the government. We don't accept the characterisation and the allegations that you have made. 

This is coming from a Labor opposition that is currently in administration. This is coming from a party that is beholden to and taking advice, directions, and instructions from Canberra. This is the credibility of the Labor opposition to come forward in the week after the budget Estimates with these allegations; it is not in keeping with due process. We still have not had an alternative budget from state Labor. This has been ongoing. They've confirmed today that that's not happening. The minister concerned has made it very clear he sees a future for the North Launceston Football Club. He's made commitments in that regard. He's made commitments to the fact there's an annual general meeting this week. He's identified the fact he's recently met with the president and he's doing the hard work that's required of the minister. We don't accept that in any way, shape, or form.

With respect to the efforts of our government regarding integrity and the efforts to reform these systems in Tasmania, it's very substantial. I've had meetings and provided briefings across the parliament in terms of our Integrity Commission reforms and they're a very substantial, large body of reforms. In terms of integrity, we're getting on with the job. We've tabled, as you know, through you, Deputy Speaker, the mandatory notifications legislation to strengthen our response to the commission of inquiry. We have 191 recommendations that have been made and we're in the process of implementing those recommendations. 

In addition to that, we're responding to the honourable William Cox review and his report and recommendations, and I've already committed, on the public record, to our plan to release that draft legislation for comment over the summer period and into early next year. That will include not just the commission of inquiry report and recommendations part thereof, but the Cox review and part of that, as well as the Weiss review, which the government's already on the record of committing to, particularly with respect to police and police investigations. We're getting on with the job. We've got a very large body of reform agenda in terms of integrity, in terms of being open and transparent and we're getting on with it. I've been in briefings in recent weeks with members of the crossbench. I've offered briefings to all in this place and indeed upstairs, with respect to the legislative agenda, so we're getting on with it.

I do want to take the opportunity to congratulate on the record Robert Hay KC, the new Chief Commissioner of the Integrity Commission. I thank him for his commitment and to his hard work and his future hard work for and on behalf of the Integrity Commission. It's a very senior appointment and I look forward to that. More recently, of course, public consultation in terms of RTIs and in terms of the ministerial diaries with respect to disclosures and progressing in that regard: we haven't heard much from the Labor opposition whether they wish to be part of that process in terms of transparency measures. What does the Labor opposition say about their diaries and the transparency for disclosing shadow ministerial diaries? It will be interesting to hear their contribution, perhaps during this debate today on the matter of public importance, because that's a commitment we've given as a government to doing more in this space and we're getting on with the job.

[11.35 a.m.]
Mr BAYLEY (Clark) - Honourable Deputy Speaker, I start by saying what we've heard here this morning and in budget Estimates about minister Duigan's conduct is deeply concerning. The minister's been caught red-handed punishing a community organisation simply for looking to make sure their future would be secured regardless of who formed government. It really is an indictment on this minister that he won't just apologise and stump up. If he had integrity, that's what he would do. It's an indictment on this government and on the Premier that there hasn't been an intervention to make sure that that happens.

Unfortunately, this isn't the first time we've seen the political weaponisation of taxpayer money by this government. We've seen pork barrelling by this government at a gross scale at successive elections. We've seen money secretly awarded to organisations without any proper process, seemingly purely because of the personal relationships involved. There's also a range of outstanding questions about the integrity of members of this government. 

We know that there are two longstanding Integrity Commission investigations into MPs and these have dragged on for three years. In fact, the Integrity Commission recently confirmed that one of these investigations had been delayed because the MP under investigation told the commission that they couldn't have access to their records due to parliamentary privilege. That is remarkable. As the commission has pointed out, even Adam Brooks - or Terry Brooks, it might have been - cooperated fully with their investigations into him. Now we have an MP who has apparently refused to do the same. We have to wonder what that MP is trying to hide. Did they make that decision based on legal advice? If so, did the taxpayer cover that legal advice? We sure hope not, but who knows? What we do know is that the taxpayer has paid for hundreds of thousands of dollars of legal fees for government MPs.

There is a complete lack of transparency about who this money is being spent on or why it is being spent. In trying to get to the bottom of this issue in budget Estimates, the Greens asked every minister if they'd been involved in Supreme Court matters and if they had received taxpayer funds to cover their legal fees. Despite some attempts from Mr Jaensch at interfering with those questions, we actually got straight answers from almost every single minister. It's a rare occasion that you get a straight answer in this place but, in this case, we did across the board, with one notable and concerning exception. 

Every other minister engaged with our questions and provided answers, but minister Howlett completely refused to do so. This refusal begs the question: why? Why is minister Howlett unable to say whether she's involved in Supreme Court proceedings? Every other minister clearly said that they were not. Surely, she would say the same if there was nothing to see here. Why won't minister Howlett tell us if she's had legal fees covered by the taxpayer? It's public money, its public interest, but no answers. 

There's no justification for not answering these questions, as shown by the example set by other ministers, in particular minister Ogilvie. Minister Ogilvie was in the awkward position of having to admit that she'd had some of her legal fees paid for by the taxpayer, yet she didn't dodge the question: to her credit. We don't know why she's had these costs covered and we call on the minister to provide that information. At least she fessed up to the basic fact, there was some transparency, and it was welcome. This is public money, and the public has a right to know. Instead, Tasmanians are still being kept in the dark. 

The Greens are really concerned about this lack of transparency because, in our experience, when the Liberals are trying to hide something, when the Liberals are playing secret squirrel, there's usually something to worry about. That's why we are saying that minister Howlett should answer these questions. Has she been the subject of, or a party to, a Supreme Court matter? Has she had legal fees covered by the taxpayer? 

It's why we're calling on the government to provide the bare minimum of transparency by giving us the full list of MPs who have had the taxpayer fund their lawyers, how much has been spent on each of them, and the reasons why. 

Members - Hear, hear.

[11.39 a.m.]
Mrs GREENE (Bass) - Deputy Speaker, the most important currency that a minister holds is integrity, but the behaviour of the honourable member for Windermere, Nick Duigan, that we have witnessed shows that he has none. Tasmanians deserve a minister who is up to the job, not someone who is out of their depth in a car park puddle. 

The Minister for Sport, the honourable Nick Duigan, has admitted to withdrawing $100,000 of funding from the North Launceston Football Club, not because the club failed to meet eligibility criteria, not because of governance issues, not because of merit or community need or fairness, but because they had the audacity to meet with Labor during the election. 

Let's call it for what it is: it was political retribution, it was punishment, intimidation and it was vindictive. It was a message to every organisation in this state that this government will only fund you if you abide by their political rules. That is disgraceful and it's an abuse of power. Every Tasmanian should be furious. I tell you that the players and the club members at North Launceston Football Club are furious. A commitment made in writing after months of discussions with the club gone in a flash because club president, Adrian Hall, met with Labor during the election. If that is not political punishment, then what is? If that is not ministerial misconduct, then what is?

North Launceston is not just any club. It's one of Tasmania's most historic and successful sporting institutions. For 103 years, it has called York Park home. It has supported young people, families, volunteers and community pathways. Its contribution to health, connection and pride cannot be overstated. Apparently none of that matters to the honourable member for Windermere. In his world, what determines whether a club gets support isn't need or community value or fairness, it's whether they can stay safely within his political good-books. That is not democracy, that is not integrity, and that is not how government funding should ever work.

He even said in Estimates that he doesn't know what the club wants. Well, here's the kicker - and the part that would almost be funny if it wasn't so ridiculous. His office is right across the road. He could pick up the phone, he could walk across the road, but he hasn't done that. He did meet with them last week. About time. I'm sure that was very welcome by the club. I met with them earlier in the week and they were pretty unhappy when I met with them.

The people that he financially kneecapped are directly in his line of sight from his office. He can see the impact of his decision from his desk window. He must be too ashamed to go outside. I would be because the people who he has punished are his neighbours. 

Sport is meant to unite our communities. It's meant to transcend politics, but the Minister for Sport has dragged community sport into the gutter of partisan payback, sending a message to every club, every league, every association across Tasmania that if you meet with the wrong people then your funding might disappear. If funding can be taken away from a respected community institution with a century-long legacy just because they're meeting with the wrong people, then who is next? Which business, which school, which community organisation, which council, which citizen? What kind of government does that? What kind of minister thinks that this is acceptable behaviour? I will tell you: a minister who is out of his depth. A minister who has no business controlling public funding and no business sitting in the Cabinet.

Let me make it crystal clear: he should resign and if he will not resign, then the Premier should remove him because this is not just the failure of one minister, this is the failure of leadership from Premier Jeremy Rockliff.

If the Premier truly cared, he would do something about it. We challenged him to do that this morning - to have an investigation. If he truly believed that taxpayer money should be used for communities rather than to enforce political obedience, he would not tolerate this behaviour for one single day. 

I look forward to the honourable member for Bass, Michael Ferguson's contribution on this because I hope that he will do the right thing for the club. I really hope that he will. I hope that Rob Fairs and Bridget Archer do the same because this is a matter of integrity. It is very important.

Time expired.

Amanda

That's the email that arrived. Then the letter, in writing, to the club outlining that the Liberal Party would commit to $100,000 to sort out a future for the North Launceston Football Club - in writing. When I spoke to Mr Hall ahead of Estimates, Mr Hall fully expected that commitment was still there. The reason I asked the question was to make sure it was actually happening. No-one was more surprised at the answer given by Mr Duigan than I was. Frankly, I was shocked when he said the answer. Here's what I asked. I said, 'Can you confirm that before the election you provided a draft letter to the president of the North Launceston Football Club, Adrian Hall, that included: 

I'm pleased to advise that a re-elected Tasmanian Liberal government will commit $100,000 to enable design and planning work to be undertaken around a proposed new facility for North Launceston Football Club. 

'Is that the case?' I asked the minister. He said, 'Yes.' So, I said, 'You provided a draft letter but not a final signed letter - so is the government committed to providing that $100,000 towards the upgrade, or not? 

Mr Duigan said:

I believe Mr Hall, shortly after I sent him that letter, went out and stood next to you, as you provide an alternative for him and, on the basis of that, I chose not to sign the letter.

Their commitment was there, in writing, and because he then went and stood with Labor, they pulled the money. They pulled the cash - not for any reason of policy or reason of a future for the club. They pulled it because he did media with Labor.

The club, and Mr Hall, fully expected, when I spoke to him ahead of Estimates, that the club was still being funded with $100,000. The reason I asked the question was to check it for him. The answer I got back was that no, they'd pulled the funding. They pulled the funding because he did media with Labor. It is disgraceful.

The member for Bass, in one of the few things he said that was accurate, was around the accuracy of statements that need to be made in this place. What he didn't say, though, is that ministers are held to account by a code of conduct for ministers. The code of conduct for ministers is very clear: fairness of decision making, on page 7, for most of you who probably haven't read it, including the Premier.

Ministers must take all reasonable steps to observe relevant standards of procedural fairness in decisions made by them. Such decisions are to be unaffected by bias or irrelevant considerations.

An irrelevant consideration is the fact that they did media with Labor, and because he did media with Labor, the government has now pulled the funding for that club. Why is the club homeless? Because the government forgot to include the North Launceston Football Club, that has been there for 100 years, in the York Park plans for the future. They spent $130 million on that facility and forgot the key tenant. Now they have no future at that site.

Here's the future for them, and here's the real issue and why it affects people at the North Launceston Football Club and participation in sport all over Bass. Because this hasn't been funded in this year's Budget, I don't see how the timelines work to actually give that club a future when they are kicked out of York Park. That is something that will affect young people, young players, everyone at that club. One of the most successful, famous clubs in Tasmania lost its funding because they did media with the opposition. Shameful.

Then the approach to come in here and say that, actually, it's Labor's fault, not just by the member for Bass, Mr Ferguson, but also by the Independent member for Franklin, to turn this into a Labor thing. This is a clear, cut and dried issue of integrity, where a breach of the code of conduct has been made by a minister; and we have a Premier who will not stand up to his ministers and will not uphold his own code of conduct for ministers.

Time expired.

Ms FINLAY (Bass - Deputy Leader of the Opposition) (by leave) - Honourable Speaker. I table the two letters referred to throughout Estimates, Question Time and the matter of public importance. The first letter is an email sent on 3 July 2025 to the President of the North Launceston Football Club, Adrian Hall.
